## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to chemical kinetics, focusing on the rate of change of concentration A over time t in a chemical reaction. Possible physical relationships between variables may involve reaction rates, activation energies, or mass action laws.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (rate is constant over time)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A (rate is proportional to concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate is proportional to concentration squared)
- First-order irreversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 / t) * A (rate is proportional to concentration and temperature-dependent term)
- Mass action law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * B**c2 (rate is proportional to concentrations and reaction orders)
- Monod kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (rate is proportional to concentration and saturation term)
- Power-law scaling: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (rate is proportional to concentration and time-dependent term)
- Laidler-Sachs equation: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A) (rate is proportional to concentration and two-parameter saturation term)
- Gompertz equation: dA_dt = c0 * A * ln(c1 / (c2 + A)) (rate is proportional to concentration and logarithmic term)
- Loeb-Schriter equation: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 * exp(c2 / A)) (rate is proportional to concentration and exponential term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Oscillatory behavior with frequency-dependent decay â†’ Periodic function or damped sine function
- Desensitization/half-life decay â†’ Power-law or rational fraction decays
- Fast initial phase â†’ Dirac delta or impulse function, or switching from one reaction rate to another
- Saturation behavior â†’ Rational fraction or tanh-like saturation term, x/(c1+x)
- Complex reaction mechanisms â†’ Rational fraction or power-law terms with multiple parameters
- Presence of activation energy â†’ Exponential term, exp(-c*t) or exp(c1/t)
- Non-uniform rates â†’ Piecewise functions, with intervals having different reaction rates
